    Order read for resumption of debate on motion moved by the Prime Minister and on the amendment moved by the Member for Queenstown.

    Mr Speaker: We will get on with the debate on item No. 3 of the Order Paper, the debate to range over not only the main motion hut also over the amendment. Dr Goh.

    The Minister for Finance (Dr Goh Keng Swee): Mr Speaker, Sir, I wish to confine myself only to certain remarks made by the Member for Queenstown in his speech on the Yang di-Pertuan Negara's speech. I am concerned with that portion of his speech dealing with Malaysia.

    Sir, the Barisan Sosialis, as the leading Communist front organisation in Singapore, has "fought" Malaysia, though the campaign conducted has not been as skilful as it should have been. They have lost the open confrontation which culminated in the referendum last September. The Member for Queenstown is now trying to pretend that they did not really lose the referendum. He said yesterday that if only Members of this Assembly would accept the result of the Nanyang students' so-called academic research project carried out in Tanjong Pagar and Kreta Ayer, then we would be persuaded that the people of Singapore were indeed against merger and Malaysia. But, Sir, I am not going to waste the time of the House in rebutting arguments as feeble, as foolish and as futile as the Member for Queenstown has advanced on this issue.

    I come to the main substance of his argument, and it consists of this. He said that for the immediate future, the constitutional development in Singapore

Column: 365

would consist of the immediate and unconditional release of the Communist agents and sympathisers who were detained by the Internal Security Council last February. Then after the release of these persons, the general elections should be held. The elected Government which he actually hoped would be the Barisan Sosialis Government would then re-open with the British Government the whole subject of the constitutional future of Singapore, and Malaysia presumably would then be abandoned.

    Sir, that is his idea of democratic, constitutional progress in Singapore. Needless to say, that is not our idea of democratic, constitutional progress in Singapore. The subject of detainees will be debated in a subsequent motion and I shall say no more about this. But I think it is fair for me to remind him of certain words which I said to him more than a year and a half ago, when I warned him of the consequences of willingly supporting the Communist cause. It is no use for the Member for Queenstown to pretend that there are no Communists in Singapore or that, in his own words, "the whole thing is a myth and a bogey". We are entitled to assume, in view of his age and his apparently sober and sane demeanour, that he is capable of rational judgment on the basis of facts which are known and acknowledged by everyone. If, on the face of all this, he continues his fairy tale that he does not know that his Party was and still is the major open-front political instrument for the Malayan Communist Party, then we must draw the inevitable conclusion that of his own free will and choice he supports their cause.

    Now, as I have said, the next stage of Singapore's political development, as he envisages it, is the unconditional and immediate release of the Communist agents and sympathisers, and this is to be followed by the general elections and the re-opening of the whole issue of merger and Malaysia.

    Sir, he knows, and any sane man in Singapore must know, that this is not

Column: 366

going to happen - merger and Malaysia will proceed as scheduled, namely, on the 31st of August this year. The newly independent State of the Federation of Malaysia will be proclaimed.

    Now, what will then happen? In the words of the Member for Queenstown - and here I quote from page 52 [col. 196] of yesterday's Hansard:

    `Should Britain so unwisely still impose Malaysia on the people against their will it can only last so long as there are British bayonets and jets around.'

    Now, Sir, let us ponder on the meaning and significance of these words. There are two points which come to the mind. The first is that Malaysia is to be imposed by force upon the people. We already know that this is completely untrue. In Singapore a referendum has been held and the judgment of the people is clear beyond doubt. Elsewhere the Parties in support of Malaysia have won a great majority of seats contested in local elections and the constituted governments of all the territories which constitute Malaysia are committed to bring about the establishment of Malaysia on schedule. Therefore, to say that Malaysia will have to be imposed against the will of the people is literally untrue. But there is a most sinister significance of these words which I shall explain later.

    The second point is that this possible imposition of Malaysia can only be carried out by British force of arms. If I understand the meaning of words, what the Member for Queenstown is saying is that there would be violent opposition to Malaysia and violence of such a nature that it has to be restrained by the use of military power. And this is the only possible construction that one can put on his words, for just in the succeeding sentence after the one that I quoted, he said:

    "But this will mean a heavy price in blood...".

    Sir, the Member for Queenstown is the Chairman of the Barisan Sosialis. We have the Chairman of a major political Party in Singapore saying quite bluntly and in so many words that bloodshed will follow upon the establishment of Malaysia. These are serious

Column: 367

words. They are not words uttered by students or intellectuals or ordinary men in the course of a carefree conversation. They are not words uttered in the heat of discussion. They are not words spoken under the influence of alcohol. They are words openly and solemnly uttered in the course of an important debate in the Legislative Assembly on matters of national policy. We are therefore entitled to draw the inevitable inference.

    Indeed, as we read further on in page 52 [col. 198] of Hansard we find in the penultimate sentence the Member for Queenstown saying:

    `If the last door to constitutional struggle is closed to the people, then there can remain but one final answer.'

    Now, Sir, the last door to the constitutional struggle - Malaysia - has been closed. There is no way by which the Barisan Sosialis, or any other Communist front organisation, can stop the formation of Malaysia by constitutional methods. Therefore, in the words of the Member for Queenstown, there can remain but one answer, the final answer. What answer, Mr Speaker? The only final answer in this context is quite clear, namely, the unconstitutional methods of violence and bloodshed.

    Sir, the threat is unmistakable. He is saying in effect, "Stop Malaysia now or else he prepared for violence and bloodshed," and these are words spoken in a solemn policy statement in the Singapore Legislative Assembly by the Chairman of a major political Party. We are therefore entitled to take his words at their face value.

    It is a curious feature that in the newspaper reports of his speech this morning very little prominence was given to this part of his speech in the English language newspapers. Perhaps the English language newspapers may not he aware of the full implications of this statement. But the Chinese language newspapers did not miss the point and published this part of his speech practically verbatim. There was even a minor headline attached to the report.

Column: 368

And so we can take it that the strong and tough men behind the Barisan Sosialis, the shop stewards and the tough characters in the pro-Barisan unions, will read this speech in the Chinese papers and will draw their conclusions, and that conclusion is that if Malaysia proceeds, then the Barisan Socialis and all the other open front Communist, as well as underground Communist, organisations will resort to violence. Now, Sir, if this interpretation is incorrect, let the other Members of the Barisan Sosialis in this Chamber say so unequivocably, let them denounce the Chairman for his criminal stupidity in threatening violence. It is no use for them to say that what the Member for Queenstown is saying is that there might be a risk of a spontaneous outburst of violence. Outbursts of violence in Singapore, as we all know through bitter experience, have never been spontaneous. Violence is calculated and organised and prearranged. In this instance, it is very clear, on the admission of the Chairman of the Barisan Sosialis himself, where the centre of organised violence will be.

    Sir, let me tell the Member for Queenstown - unfortunately he is not here but perhaps his colleagues will pass on the message intended for him - the great import of his words. If he resorts to violence, he must expect the constituted Government of Malaysia to resort to adequate counter measures to contain such violence and to apprehend the criminals responsible for such violence and bring them to justice.

    So long as the Barisan Sosialis and other Communist front organisations are content to use non-violent methods of subversion, then the worst penalty that they can expect will be a period of detention until such time as they are persuaded of the follies of their ways. But when there is a resort to violence, punishment is not merely detention in gaol either in Singapore or the Federation, punishment is death by hanging. Not only the immediate perpetrators of violence will suffer this fate, but those who are responsible for inciting and organising them will also have to pay this ultimate price.

Column: 369



    Sir, it is not for the Member for Queenstown to say that death by hanging meted out te perpetrators of violence constitutes Fascist or undemocratic methods. Armed revolt against any constituted government amounts to treasonable action, and in any democratic government the penalty for such a crime of treason is death.

    Sir, we have to accept also that with such momentous words being uttered, the policy statement of the Chairman of the Barisan Sosialis has been cleared and has been accepted by all his colleagues in the Party leadership. Therefore, both they and he will be jointly and severally responsible for the consequences of such a policy. I make this observation, Mr Speaker, Sir, because there are moments when I tell that the Barisan Sosialis open front leadership, as distinct from the real and effective underground direction, consists of eccentric lunatics or ill-tempered maladjusted social misfits, or just downright imbeciles and idiots. Sometimes I gather the impression that they behave like Little children playing with sand castles on the beaches, not knowing what they do, why they are doing it, nor the serious consequences that could follow from their action. It is because I get the impression that they sometimes do not understand the grave implications of their actions that on various occasions I bring upon myself, at grave risk of being misunderstood, the duty of pointing out to them the dire consequences that must follow upon their proposed line of action.

    Dr Toh Chin Chye: Mr Speaker, the referendum held last year is now seven months old. It is accepted in the minds of the people that Malaysia will be established on 31st August, in spite of the Barisan Sosialis conspiracy to abort Malaysia with the assistance of foreign opposition. Therefore, when the Member for Queenstown keeps on talking of Malaysia as an imperialist and neo-colonialist plot, and that the Borneo territories have no affinity with Malaya and should be returned to Indonesia, he betrays the mental groove into which the Barisan Sosialis has fallen. It is a tragedy for Members of the

Column: 370

Barisan Sosialis when their leaders cannot reorientate their political thinking and persist in playing a worn-out record of Malaysia being a camouflage for British colonialism.

    The prediction of the Chairman of the Barisan Sosialis that there will be bloodshed when Malaysia is established will no doubt be duly noted by those who are responsible for the safety and security of this country. It is said that "prevention is better than cure", and I have no doubt that prophylactic measures will be taken to prevent such bloodshed occurring.

    The Member for Queenstown talks of poverty, disease, ignorance and want. There is no one in Singapore who is so poor that he cannot have his daily meals of rice. The per capita income of Singapore is $1,300, which is the highest in the Far East. There is no epidemic which afflicts the people: the standards of our public health and hospital care have made Singapore one of the healthiest places to live in. There is free primary education for children of all races and we are already expending 23 per cent of our budget on education. If there are poverty, disease, ignorance and want, they exist only amongst the Barisan Sosialis. But here I must make a clear definition. I cannot say that the leaders of the Barisan Sosialis are materially poor. Their poverty is a mental poverty caused by their inability to free themselves from Communist cliches, and their blindness to the real political situation which faces us today. The poverty of their political thinking and ignorance of the real needs of the people have brought upon them a disease in which everything they see is only of one colour.

    After merger and Malaysia have been established, the anti-colonial cry will only be an echo of the past.

    We are entering into a new phase in which is required leadership with positive ideas and plans, which will advance not only the material welfare of the people of Singapore but also the development of Malaysia. A country which has previously been subject to colonialism inevitably throw up a type

Column: 371

of militant leadership which is uncompromising in its tight against foreign domination. With Malaysia this phase of the battle is past and gone. A re-adjustment of political thought becomes necessary. The old anti-colonialism war cries will not cause manna to fall from heaven or turn stones into bread. Nor will cries of "Bersatu" create more jobs. Only by careful planning and by the sweat of our brows can we hope to maintain the high living standards that we enjoy in Singapore and generally in Malaysia.

    The climate of Singapore is now one of construction. Energy and time previously frittered away in political excitement have been devoted to intense work and construction. The fruits of these labours have been detailed in the Yang di-Pertuan Negara's speech. The intense building activity of the Housing and Development Board, the Public Works Department and private builders is changing the skyline of Singapore.

    Jurong, once upon a time an evil-smelling marsh, has been converted into an industrial estate. Land is being reclaimed in the East lagoon and new wharves will be built. Television Singapura though barely two months old has been a whacking success and will no doubt in time to come make an impact upon the pattern of living in Singapore. These are indeed achievements of which we can be proud but they have been made possible by the technical skill and ability of Singapore's workers.

    As the number of students who leave secondary and primary schools increases year by year, the pressure of jobseekers must cause concern among all these who have the welfare of our society at heart. The problem is being tackled in two directions. The first step is to stimulate capital investment in industrial enterprises so that new factories will be built and ancillary services expanded. In order to achieve this object, not only a climate of confidence in the political future of Singapore must be created but also there must be industrial peace. With

Column: 372

the participation of Singapore in Malaysia, the unsureness of our political future will disappear.

    The Economic Development Board has been the spearhead in our industrialisation programme, but if industrialisation is to succeed it is essential that there must be available in Singapore a reservoir for skilled technical manpower. For this reason, emphasis has been placed on the development of technical education. The Polytechnic is now in its fifth year and the time has now come to develop it into an institute of advanced technology. Steps are being taken to remove the Craft Courses out of the Polytechnic to Balestier and they will form the nucleus for a future vocational institute. The scope for undergraduate courses at technician and professional level will be expanded in the Polytechnic and past-graduate work will be introduced. The graduates which the Polytechnic have produced have shown their worth, particularly to employers in industry. It is now time to carry the development of the Polytechnic one stage further. We intend later in the year or next year to introduce a Bill which will enable the Polytechnic to confer degrees upon those who hold professional diplomas.

    While we are confident of maintaining the present pace of construction, we must be equally vigilant that the prosperity of Singapore now enjoyed is not destroyed at one fell stroke by an unpredictable slump in trade or a fall in the price of rubber. The reserves that have been accumulated, and to which considerable reference has been made by the Opposition during this debate, are a useful asset for the wintry days should there be a short-fall in revenue and development funds which are hard to come by. I am quite sure Members of the House will agree that we ought never to live like Micawber - ï¿½10 income, ï¿½11 expenditure.

    Finally, Mr Speaker, may I add that it is not because of impiety that we have failed to thank God in the Yang di-Pertuan Negara's speech, as the Lady from Mountbatten would have us do. I am sure God will be more pleased if

Column: 373

we spend less time thanking him in political speeches and more time rolling up our sleeves and getting down to work.

    Mr Speaker: The Prime Minister in reply.

    The Prime Minister: Mr Speaker, Sir, just formally to close the debate on the Motion of thanks to the Yang di-Pertuan Negara's speech. Over the last two days I think the Assembly itself has reflected a new mood and Members find it difficult to get exuberant or really angry over anything. A certain finality prevails over everything and I think it is to the good that everybody in this country, including Members on the Opposition Benches, understands that there is a finality in the state of things in Singapore and in Malaysia.

    As to the way we have discharged our duties in Singapore, I leave it to concrete evidence - and literally concrete, bricks, stones, cement, girders - to bear testimony to some of the work we have done over the last 3ï¿½ years and will continue to do between now and 31st August. After 31st August, Mr Speaker, Sir, a new phase opens and perhaps when that time comes we will chart briefly, again before you, what we think lies ahead. But I think, like all good thrillers, one must never anticipate. We have enough to keep everybody happy and contented between now and 31st August. I hope Members on the other side will take my words to heart that the 1st September really settled a lot of things and that it will be utter folly to go on - as the Member for Queenstown yesterday went on - fighting that verdict. For him to suggest that North Borneo, which does not belong to him but belongs to the people of Malaysia, should be given away to some foreign power. I think that is the sign of reckless foolhardiness which is bound to end up with a great deal more unhappiness all round. All I can say is that, every time after the event, like Cassandra, more in sorrow than in anger, we have pleaded, albeit in vain.

    Question put, "That the words proposed to be added, be there added."

INTERNAL SECURITY COUNCIL'S
DECISION AND STATEMENT ON
COMMUNIST CONSPIRACY


10.12 p.m.

    The Prime Minister: Mr Speaker, Sir, I rise to move the motion,

    That this House supports the decision of the Internal Security Council made by representatives of the three Governments - the United Kingdom. Singapore and the Federation of Malaya - on the 1st February. 1963, ordering that certain persons known to the security authorities of the three Governments to be deeply implicated in the Communist United Front conspiracy to jeopardise national defence and security of Singapore and the territories of the proposed Federation of Malaysia, should be arrested immediately and not left till after 31st August, 1963, and that it endorses the statement made by the Internal Security Council as contained in Paper Misc. 2 of 1963.

    On the 1st of February, the Internal Security Council met in Kuala Lumpur. It decided that action should be taken immediately to safeguard national defence and security of Singapore and of the other territories of Malaysia. It decided that certain - not all - of those known to the three Security Authorities to he deeply implicated in the United Front working for Communist and foreign interests must be arrested.

    In the early hours of Saturday morning, the 2nd of February, operations were launched from Johore by Singapore and Federation Special Branch officers and a number of persons were detained. I do not think the public were surprised at the action taken against these Communists and their United Front workers. For that matter, the Communists were not surprised either.

    Perhaps a word of explanation, Mr Speaker, Sir. Since it is rather late in the evening, it is inadvisable to drink tea and it is better to drink water. To those Members of the Opposition Benches who find it difficult to keep awake in the evening, I recommend Chinese tea, particularly the Member for Queenstown.

    In 1956, when Mr Lim Ching Siong and his Communist United Front friends were taken to gaol, the action was accompanied by riots and civil

Column: 376

commotion. This was because the Communists had then succeeded in creating an issue over Chinese education and in exploiting a series of strikes. Thousands of Chinese students camping at the Chung Cheng and Chinese High Schools - Eton and Harrow for a lot of Chinese parents in Malaysia - were broken up by tear-gas. They marched down Bukit Timah Road with arms linked, in tears particularly because of the tear-gas. The action against the students gave the Communists a chance to claim that they were defending Chinese civilisation, education and culture. As a result, an air of martyrdom was assumed by these Communist detainees. They appeared to be defenders of Chinese culture and champions of the workers. This time, on the contrary, the detention of these Communists has not caused any surprise, let alone consternation, amongst the public. On the contrary, there is an air of calm and tranquility. Instead of broken shop-windows and barbed wire and troops, there is peace and business as usual.

    The Communists wanted an emergency meeting of their United Front cadres, wanted an emergency sitting of this Assembly in the hope of whipping up excitement and tensions, all under cover of privilege. However, because the Member for Cairnhill, for his own reasons, also asked for it, we agreed. Unfortunately, as you have ruled, no emergency sitting could be held until the new Session opened. We offered them radio forums. They declined.

    Sir, we are always prepared to meet them in the open and join issue with them. We have nothing to hide, nothing to fear, and, as Members know, for nearly two years now, we have had a continuous and open debate with the Communists over merger and Malaysia and Singapore's non-Communist future as part of Malaysia or, as the Internal Security Council says it, "whether it should become a Cuba."

    Before Lim Ching Siong, leading the open front organisations, embarked on this reckless adventure of trying to make Singapore a Cuba, even at the risk of selling it to foreign powers in this region,

Column: 377

he took instructions from the Communist underground.

    The day following the Anson by-election - Sunday, 16th July, 1961 - Lim Cling Siong made contact with the underground Communist Party of Malaya for instructions. This contact was made in the Nee Soon area at the 7ï¿½ mile, Upper Thomson Road, in a house off the main road. A number of other senior cadres, including Chok Koh Tong and Tan Hee Kim - being leading members of the Barisan Sosialis - were gathered at the place when discussions were held. Arrangements for the meeting were completely clandestine. At 1927 hours, Lim left the Singapore General Employees Union in Middle Road for the corner of Outram Road and Seng Poh Road, opposite the Chung Khiaw Bank Branch there. He walked to the five-foot way, and at about 1938 hours, a black Morris Minor SR. 5222 drew up. There were two male Chinese in the vehicle ---

    Mr Bani: He did not ---

    The Prime Minister: Perhaps the Member for Thomson could contain himself. He will know that from time to time that car - [Interruption]

    Mr Speaker: Order.

    The Prime Minister: - is seen in the precincts of this House. [Interruption]

    Mr Speaker: Order.

    The Prime Minister: Yes, indeed. I do not think the Member for Toa Payoh thinks it is very funny.

    Mr Wong Soon Fong (Toa Payoh): No.

    Mr Speaker: Order.

    The Prime Minister: There were two male Chinese in the vehicle, one of whom was Chok Koh Tong. Lim, by this time, had put on a pair of dark glasses in the evening. He got into the car quickly which then drove off at great speed. He and Chok were dropped off at the bus-stop, 7ï¿½ milestone Thomson Road, and the car drove off to the Work Brigade Barracks, Andrews

Column: 378

Avenue, Sembawang. The meeting in the house at Sembawang went on throughout the night and into the early hours of the morning.

    After this important discussion, these senior cadres, including Lim, held a series of meetings amongst themselves to work out the details of a plan to be implemented straightaway.

    Sir, the Communists preferred Singapore not to merge with the Federation. They wanted to make it into a Cuba from which they hoped to mount an offensive against the Federation of Malaya. When they lost the referendum last September and the overwhelming majority of us - the people - voted decisively for merger, for a peaceful and stable future in Malaysia, they knew that their fate was sealed. They knew that after the 31st of August, they will face security action. The first team of open leaders were well known and could not withdraw and go into hiding. Also, if they had done this, their rank and file would have lost heart and melted away. So their first team of open united front cadres in the political Parties, unions, rural associations and cultural organisations had to be sacrificed. The Communists treated them as expendables to be sacrificed. However, there were other less well-known expendables - the reserve team - cadres whose names and faces were less well known to the public. These, the Communists had hoped, could escape action when the first team was removed. They could go into hiding, since they were not so well known. Their plan was that when the first team had gone after the purge, and some time had elapsed and things looked safe, they could come out and take over the key positions left vacant by their first team, and carry on the conspiracy, restarting and re-forming the united front. Of course, the three Governments knew of this and as the reserve team withdrew and took cover, intelligence men followed to keep track of them. In some cases, however, they have not as yet been found. No doubt after some time, when they think it is safe, they will come out and resume their activities.

Column: 379



    But Lim Ching Siong and his friends prepared for trouble. They knew what they were doing was wrong. They knew they were deliberately defying the will of the people expressed clearly in the referendum and they were plotting with Azahari to frustrate Malaysia.

    When they failed to stop Malaysia through Singapore, they began to look around for ways and means to stop Malaysia through fellow Communists in the S.U.P.P. in Sarawak. They even plotted with an anti-Communist adventurer like Azahari in Brunei. They knew that without the Borneo territories the Tunku would not agree to Malaysia. So they plotted in various was to create trouble in the Borneo territories to stop merger between Singapore and the Federation. To achieve this, Said Zahari, a former editor of Utusan Melayu, who was banned from the Federation in 1961 after the Utusan strike, played a great part.

    The three Governments knew that Said was Lim Ching Siong's closest Malay associate. Said was in touch with an intelligence agent of a foreign power. In fact, he was in their pay. The three Governments also knew that Said was Azahari's adviser and contact man in Singapore. Said arranged several secret meetings between Lim and Azahari. Their last meeting was four days before the revolt broke out in Brunei. Lim Ching Siong had previously discussed a request by Azahari for money to buy arms. In fact, Lim and his friends were debating whether to give Azahari the money for this purpose. But they had their misgivings about whether the money would be spent for the purchase of arms or whether it would he spent on women for Azahari.

    Hon. Members will understand from the brief summary of these facts that the Communists knowingly took the risk of action upon themselves.

    After the 16th of December last year, when action had been taken in Sarawak and the Federation of Malaya, they took special preventive measures. They knew that security actions were usually taken in the early hours of the morning

Column: 380

when people were at home. Lim Ching Siong, therefore, gave instructions to all his first team united front cadres to stay in a different place each night, so that the largest number of men might escape when the purge came. It took the police a great deal of trouble and men to mark out the different places where each of these people stayed in the course of one week. Some of them had as many as four or five different places in a week.

    Lim himself and some leading lights in the Barisan Sosialis, including several hon. Members on the other side, took special precautions. They believed that since the security action in the Federation and Sarawak had been taken in the early hours of Sunday morning, so every Saturday night they went to a midnight show, so that they would not get home till well after two or three o'clock on the Sunday morning. In this way, they would hear of any action that may already have been started and so have time to dive for cover and elude the police.

    The operations were mounted with great secrecy from Johore. Yet, in spite of the strict security, partly because of their early counter measures, like withdrawing their reserve team and getting their first team to change their sleeping places each night, some 18 of their important first team members could not be found, and quite a number of their reserve team who had taken cover could not be traced.

    Many Members may ask why security action was taken on 1st February, 1963, instead of some other time, like after 31st August, 1963. Well, there were urgent reasons why it had to he taken in the early hours of the morning of 2nd February. An important member of the Communist united front, Said Zahari, was leaving that morning for Jakarta where Azahari had just arrived the day before from Manila. The last time when intelligence reports came to the notice of the Federation Government of an impending revolt in Brunei by persons trained in Indonesian Borneo, no action was taken. The Tunku said that, although he informed the British, they did not take sufficient preventive steps. British Intelligence did

Column: 381

not altogether accept the imminence of the danger. In retrospect now, had the report been acted on, perhaps the Brunei revolt, which has cost a lot of money, involved movements of troops and arms, caused deaths and built up an atmosphere of crisis with some of our neighbours, may not have happened.

    This time, however, none of the three Governments on the Internal Security Council was willing to be caught napping. And partly because the security action has been successful, the things which were being planned have not taken place. A part of the plan was to mount demonstrations and violent protests in Singapore at the same time as so-called "volunteers" were moved to renew the revolt in Brunei.

    There are three Governments on the Internal Security Council, and the Intelligence information available to the Security Council was derived from three intelligence agencies.

    I am in a position to disclose only information collected by the Singapore security organisation and part of the information collected by the Federation security organisation. The British do not wish to disclose their Intelligence information, particularly information from their Intelligence sources in the capitals of South-East Asian countries. They have their reasons for not wanting to disclose information which may jeopardise their sources and may, even worse, make their position vis-a-vis certain powers in South-East Asia more difficult. Each of the three Governments on the Security Council has different immediate interests, and the British have different long-term objectives from the Federation Government and us. But nevertheless, all of us were agreed on the need for immediate action. For one thing, Sir, at that time, the Singapore Communists were making veiled threats to resort to violent struggle.

    As recently as the 1st January this year Mr Lim Ching Siong, in his New Year message, said:

    `The ruling clique in the Federation is heavily committed to the imperialists and will pursue an anti-democratic policy in the hope of maintaining themselves in power indefinitely'.

Column: 382

Then he ominously said:

    'The Left forces must then make the necessary judgment on the matter.'

    Now, what is the meaning of this? Members will remember that every now and then Barisan Sosialis leaders have made similar statements. They have done so many times in this Chamber and did so again yesterday. To us who have known the Communists for so long, and studied their thinking and their methods, the meaning is clear. They will use constitutional methods as long as these are useful to them. At the same time, they are ready to use more violent methods - strikes, riots, and, in the last resort, armed insurrection. These considered statements were made by persons of authority in the Communist front movement and were intended to prepare their cadres for stronger action when the time was ripe.

    On 2nd February, immediately the arrests were known, the Member for Queenstown issued a statement in which he said:

    Now is the time for the people to consider seriously whether the present arrests, and the repressive actions have not already closed all the doors to constitutional struggle,'

He repeated that again yesterday:

    `If the last door to constitutional struggle is closed, then there remains but one final answer.'

He goes on to talk of bloodshed if Malaysia were pushed through.

    The question for the Internal Security Council was when will violence be mounted - before 31st August, 1963, or after 31st August, 1963? It so happened that events in Brunei gave them another opportunity to try and stop Malaysia. Let me give hon. Members the main outline of how the Communists in Singapore tried to exploit the situation.

    Sheik Azahari is not a Communist. He is too fond of the good life. Nor are the persons immediately around him Communists. But for different reasons, he was opposed to Brunei entering Malaysia, unless it was on his terms. And the Communists saw in Azahari and the few thousand Malays be led in Brunei a convenient cover for their conspiracy. The revolt would be made to appear as the forefront of a

Column: 383

liberation movement in Borneo and so prevent the Borneo territories from joining Malaysia and without Borneo, the Tunku would not have Singapore. As luck would have it for the Communists, the Filipinos, also known to be anti-Communists, had made claims on North Borneo. Some Filipinos had discussions with Azahari last November and certain Filipino personalities established links with Azahari and settled a deal on mutually profitable terms. Here was the perfect blind, for nobody can accuse Azahari's revolt to establish the independent State of Kalimantan Utara, otherwise known as the United States of Borneo, as being a Communist conspiracy, for Azahari was not a Communist and the Filipino personalities who backed him were also known anti-Communists. But the irony is that the Communists made good use of them.

    Sir, no one will ever know how lucky we were that Azahari's revolt went off at half cock, earlier than originally planned, and flopped. Had the original plan which was co-ordinated to coincide with events outside Borneo succeeded, the Sultan captured and made to proclaim the independence of Kalimantan Utara, as may well have happened, we would all have been in a very dangerous situation. But as things turned out Sheik Azahari was no Ferhat Abbas of Algeria. Nor was he made of sterner stuff of men like Ben Bella or Ben Khedda.

    Mr Speaker: Order. I am sorry to interrupt the Prime Minister, but I think one hon. Member is using his ear-phone as a loud-speaker. Could a check be made? [Pause] It is not here. It must be up in the Strangers' Gallery. If it is in the Strangers' Gallery, I ask the Serjeant at Arms to try and trace that loud-speaker. Mr Prime Minister.

    The Prime Minister: Sir, I do not want to introduce unparliamentary language in this Chamber, but I think I am fair in quoting Azahari's lawyer in saying that he is a liar and a "bum".

Column: 384



    Long before the revolt actually took place, Lim Ching Siong bad been in regular and secret contact with Azahari. On all the visits Azahari made to Singapore during last year, Said was his closest associate and confidant.

    Mr Speaker: Order. Perhaps the Prime Minister would like to take his seat again. I am told that it is probably the loud-speaker in the Member for Anson's seat - he is not here. Mr Prime Minister.

    The Prime Minister: On several occasions Said arranged meetings between Azahari and Lim Ching Siong. Lim Ching Siong met Azahari at 11.15 on the night of 4th March, 1962, in secret at 118 Tembeling Road. They met again on the 12th of April. On the 3rd of December, just four days before the revolt, all the three, Messrs. Lim Ching Siong, Said Zahari and Azahari met at the Tiong Hwa Restaurant in Prinsep Street. Then within less than 24 hours after the outbreak of the revolt on the 8th, the Barisan Sosialis came out in open support of the revolution.

    As early as May last year, Mr Lim Ching Siong was already aware of the plans for an uprising. He was then actively considering an offer of weapons being made either in Singapore or in Borneo through his links with the S.U.P.P. He was not quite clear about the situation then prevailing in Brunei and the offer of weapons "to his side". He feared it might be a trap because he was worried that top level "fellows may betray him". He also knew that there was a promise for troops to be sent from the border at the time when the revolt was mounted.

    All this while the Communists in Singapore knew what was being hatched. In October last year, several weeks before the revolt, the three Governments knew that even Mr Mahadeva of the Straits Times, now detained, knew of the impending revolt and had told some people that Malaysia may not come off as there was going to be an armed revolt in Brunei.

    Captured rebel leaders in Brunei have revealed that Azahari had told them that he had arranged for a simultaneous uprising in Singapore at the same time as.

Column: 385

they attacked in Brunei, Sarawak and Sabah. Lim and Said had promised Azahari that they would mount demonstrations and hamper British troop movements in Singapore when counter action was taken by the British, and they promised to rally support for this so-called "revolution".

    For a number of reasons they did not succeed. A pending retrenchment of over a thousand Army civilian workers made the climate unsuitable for getting Army civilian workers to take action against base installations. Civilian employees of the Army are employed in order to keep these bases ready for an emergency. The workers were not prepared to jeopardise their rice bowl just for Communist tactics. They failed to get the workers to do things against the workers' own interests. In anger Lim issued a statement condemning the use of the British bases in Singapore in crushing the so-called "liberation" struggle of Kalimantan Utara. They also got the President of the Naval Base Labour Union, Mr De Cruz, to condemn the use of the bases in putting down the revolt. This was immediately echoed in all their other united front publications.

    They called two so-called "mass rallies" at Hollywood Park, rather inappropriately named for mass rallies, the first by the Barisan Sosialis directed at the Chinese, the second by Party Rakyat directed at the Malays. Both meetings were cold and drew small crowds. Again they failed.

    Earlier they had even tried to get arms for the rebels. On 6th December last year, two days before the revolt broke out, Azahari went in Said's car to Jalan Spencer, off West Coast Road, to meet a contact to get stolen arms.

    Said, the link between Lim Ching Siong and Azahari, was all this while in the pay of an agent of an Intelligence agent of a foreign power. He has now, under interrogation, admitted his links with them. Some time ago his agent was arrested. He disclosed that Said was in his pay. The agent was released and he returned to his own country. Shortly afterwards another man came to Singapore. He became Said's "handling agent", a technical term to describe a

Column: 386

person who keeps contact with an agent for an intelligence agency. The first agent who was arrested and released obviously did not report to his organisation that he had already revealed Said's connections with them.

    When Azahari was last in Singapore just before he fled to Manila, he was in constant touch with the leading conspirators in Singapore and also with certain persons connected with foreign consulates. Surveillance was kept on all the key conspirators.

    Shortly after the revolt in Borneo, Said secretly tried to start a movement for volunteers to fight for the liberation of Azahari's Kalimantan Utara, just like the volunteers who were going to fight for the liberation of West Irian.

    Mr Speaker, Sir, all this may sound a little bit ambitious now in retrospect, if not comic, but these men take themselves seriously, and we would have made a grave mistake if we did not take them seriously.

    These men knew that they had lost the battle in Singapore against Malaysia. So they resorted to every available device, and exploited every opportunity to create trouble in the other territories, particularly in Sarawak and Brunei, in order to stop Malaysia. Honourable Members may recall reading in the newspapers of the sudden increase in the number of Barisan Sosialis and other united front cadres who began to tour Sarawak and Brunei in the last few weeks before the revolt. Some will also remember that when the revolt broke out, they were immediately detained and expelled from Brunei and Sarawak. I do not think their capacity for harm was very great but the Sarawak and Brunei Governments did not think that they were just sight-seeing.

    After the experience of the Brunei revolt, it would be a mistake to underestimate Communist intention or capacity for harm. They had said in the past that there would be bloodshed and violence and they said again yesterday, through the Member for Queenstown, that there would be bloodshed if Malaysia came about or was pushed through, as he put it. This was said by some of their leaders now in detention,

Column: 387

Mr Lim Ching Siong, Mr Fong Swee Suan and Mr Sandra Woodhull. Yesterday the Member for Queenstown repeated this threat under the cloak of privilege. Some people did not take them seriously in the past. Events have shown that they were prepared to use the Brunei Malays and involve themselves in conspiracy with foreign groups to precipitate armed revolt in the Borneo territories to stop Malaysia. Action could not be delayed. Already relations between the Federation and neighbouring countries are gravely strained, and we can only hope that goodwill from all sides, with the help of conciliation and mediation by disinterested officials of international organisations, will ease the situation.

    Sir, the Communists did their calculations carefully. They knew that on or after 31st August, their united front would be disrupted. In their eagerness and recklessness to escape this fate, they involved themselves with persons who ii turn were involved with foreign powers. They have brought retribution upon themselves sooner than they had expected.

    It would have been easier for the Singapore Government to leave them alone until after 31st August, for then the Central Government would assume complete responsibility for defence and security, and take over direct control of the Police and Intelligence. But when the Communists threatened the security of Malaysia, we had to agree to take immediate action to curb them. Probably, as far as Singapore alone was concerned, they could not have created much trouble because they had already been discredited. After nearly two years of open confrontation and public debate the ground was growing cold for them. The Chinese education issue they mounted had failed. Last December they had to abandon their plans for another examination boycott. Their strikes were failing, and in fact only a few days before the arrests, after fierce talk and strike action at Metal Box, Mr Fong Swee Suan had to tell the workers

Column: 388

to go back with very little benefits gained and a lot of face lost. Their unions were breaking away from them.

    We have been able to hold the Communists down because we had exposed their deceit and selfishness in opposing merger and Malaysia and isolated them, by public debate and the open argument. They suffered a humiliating defeat at the hands of the people in the referendum last September. Since then we have been spared a great deal of this bragging by the Communists and their supporters in this Assembly that they had the masses behind them. We have not heard of the masses, Mr Speaker, Sir, for the last few days.

    One of the reasons why the purges of the last Government were accompanied by riots and arson, and troops had to be called out, was that Ministers of the last Government were unable or unwilling to meet the Communists in the open and argue it out. The result was that they lost the argument and lost the battle for hearts and minds. So when they detained leading figures, a lot of public sympathy was for the Communists and against the Government. We must never make this error. We are prepared to join issue with the Communists at any time, and all the time, here in this Assembly, on the radio, in T.V., in public forums, in public rallies, a, the United Nations, in Moshi, in Afro-Asian conferences, anywhere and everywhere. We have even invited the Chairman of the Movement for Colonial Freedom in London, Mr Fenner Brockway, to come here, investigate and satisfy himself about all this rubbish of so-called torture that the Member for Queenstown had told him about in his recent trip to London. I am happy to say that he will be coming, not as early as I hoped he would be able to come in April, but some time in May. The Member for Queenstown should remember this before he goes around spreading rumours and falsehoods, that this is a Government that never flinches from the open confrontation.

    It is they who fear the public debate. The Indonesian Communists and other Communist bloc delegates at the Afro-Asian Conference in Tanganyika feared

Column: 389

the arguments of our delegates. As Members know, on 1st February we sent a delegation to this conference. We knew that this conference was controlled by a Communist-dominated Secretariat. Azahari himself had said in Jakarta that the Conference was dominated by Communists and that he was not going on that account. We knew that the Communist bloc led by the Communist Party of Indonesia would try to move a resolution condemning Malaysia as neo-colonialist and giving support to Azahari as the leader of the so-called revolution in Kalimantan Utara.

    The Indonesian and other Communists were afraid of our facts and arguments, so they stubbornly opposed our delegates from even presenting the case for Malaysia before the Afro-Asian delegates.

    Mr Bani: Before Lim Shee Ping was arrested.

    Mr Rajaratnam: No papers.

    The Prime Minister: Shee Ping? A Member of this House was not aware of the reply that was given. Mr Lim Shee Ping, I fear to say, was no match when it really came to the open argument between him and the gentlemen that we sent - Mr Devan Nair, Mr Jek, Mr Rahim Ishak, Othman Wok. He went to the Polytechnic to meet the Minister for Finance and we have a tape recording of what happened, the ground went cold on him. Doctrinaire, half-baked Marxist - [Interruption].

    Mr Speaker: Order.

    The Prime Minister: This was at the Polytechnic Students' Union [Interruption]

    Mr Speaker: Order. I ask the Member for Thomson, if he wishes to intervene, to intervene in the proper way; not from his seat. Mr Prime Minister.

    The Prime Minister: No, Mr Speaker, Sir, I always allow him to intervene. I will never refuse him an opportunity as long as he is with us to debate, to argue, as long as he behaves himself in a constitutional manner. I think the Member for Thomson ought

Column: 390

to be grateful that he has a Government in power that is anxious to see that the decorum of public debates, public assemblies is somehow maintained despite very trying circumstances.

    Sir, at Moshi they knew that if our delegates were allowed to speak, they could have shown that it was nonsense to claim that Azahari's revolution of 2,000 out of 40,000 Malays in Brunei - 40,000 Malays in Brunei, meaning men, women and children and babes in arms, Mr Speaker, Sir, half the size of the Member for Geylang Serai's constituency; half the population - entitled him to proclaim himself Prime Minister, not just of Brunei, but of the 1.2 million people of Sarawak and Sabah. The Indonesian Communists wanted to rally Afro-Asian opinion against Malaysia. They will try hard first in conferences like that in Tanganyika, and if they succeed, then finally in the United Nations. The very fact that they have made no mention of this attenuated resolution that has been passed supporting Azahari's Kalimantan Utara, either by the Indonesian Communists in Jakarta or by local agents in Singapore, is an indication of the defeat they suffered at Moshi. Sir, if they could get the non-aligned countries of Afro-Asia to denounce Malaysia, it would provide for them a cover for intervention without the danger of a world war. For once non-Communist Afro-Asia supports a liberation movement, as it did in Algeria, to aid rebels in the way of arms and volunteers by other Afro-Asian powers, it cannot be easily countered by intervention by a major Western power. Then there will be no danger of its provoking a world war or leading to United States intervention.

    This was what happened in the case of West Irian. Once Afro-Asia solidly backed Indonesia, the Americans being practical persuaded the stubborn Dutchmen to give up West Trim rather than risk a war in which Afro-Asia would be against them. Sir, I do not say that Sarawak and Sabah is like West Irian. In fact, the Indonesian Communists are rapidly finding that this is a very different proposition. Sarawak, Brunei and Sabah were not part of the Dutch empire. They belong to us, the people

Column: 391

of the territories which together were part of the British empire in South-East Asia. They do not belong to the Member for Queenstown alone, and it is not his to give away to the Indonesians, as I heard he wanted to do yesterday. If Azahari claims the support of 40,000 Malays in Brunei, then there are 1.2 million people in Sarawak and Sabah who oppose him. However, we must expect the Indonesian Communists to keep on trying. Our business is to defeat their diplomatic and propaganda offensive at every turn.

    The recent security action was taken in a different situation from 1956. In 1956, when the Communists were purged, they were part of an anti-colonial united front when we nationalists in the P.A.P. were together with them fighting a common colonial enemy for our freedom. The last time, in 1956, they were purged by a Chief Secretary who was a British official. It was a semi-colonial government whose understanding and grasp of the Communist problem in an anti-colonial situation was feeble, and whose ability to counter Communist tactics was pathetic. This time they were arrested on the decision of the three Governments - the Federation of Malaya, an independent nationalist Government, the Government of Singapore, consisting all of elected Ministers, and the British Government, which has a defence treaty with the Federation of Malaya and is also responsible for the external defence of Singapore. Sir, we have different immediate policies and different political attitudes and different methods. But we all agreed with the decision of the Internal Security Council because it was vital that no chances should he taken that would upset Malaysia and because we in Singapore share vital long-term objectives with the Federation Government on the defence and security of Malaysia.

    The persons detained were known not just to one but to all three security authorities of the thee Governments to be deeply implicated in the Communist conspiracy. So there was no question of

Column: 392

political victimisation or personal vendetta. The decision on who were to be detained was an impersonal one, dispassionately made by professional security officers whose instructions from their respective Governments were to blunt the Communist capacity to mount trouble, leading perhaps to violence, and to break their lines of conspiracy with foreign groups. The decision of the I.S.C. was not immediately to destroy all Communist united front organisations. The operation had a limited objective, for a specific purpose, to meet a particular situation. So no political Party or trade union or rural association has been banned, although they are known vehicles of the Communist united front. Only those persons who were known by the three different security authorities to be deeply implicated in the conspiracy - in other words, the key activists in the political Parties, unions aid rural organisations, who were their open points for mobilising support to violent action, mobilising their workers of farmers who belong to these organisations, were detained. Because of this directive, certain other persons, although known to the security organisations to be Communist united front cadres, were not detained in this action.

    In 1956 after the purge, the Communists and their supporters felt that victory was around the corner. The P.A.P. had been fighting with them in an anti-colonial united front. They knew that when we won the general elections in 1959 and got the keys to Changi Prison, we would have to open the prison gates for them. Otherwise we would have been accused of being traitors to fellow fighters in a common anti-colonial cause. This time, Mr Speaker, Sir, they know the e is no victory around the corner. Whoever wants to open the prison gates either of Changi - there would not be Outram anymore - Pudu, Taiping or Johore, must conquer Malaya and Malaysia by force, or must constitutionally win the majority of the seats in the Malaysian Parliament. Neither of these two ways appears even remotely possible.

Column: 393



    But I think the most dangerous aspect of this limited purge of Communist front organisers is that the country may be lulled into a sense of false security. Without the leading Communist front figures in the open, without their wild postures, their fierce statements, their strikes and inflammatory speeches, people may be lulled into believing that the Communist threat is gone. Let us never deceive ourselves that this action has removed the Communist threat. Even if the Internal Security Council had arrested all the other united front cadres and banned their organisations, the problem would only be slightly diminished. The basic threat remains.

    There are two reasons for this. First, the underground party is still there. Our security organisation has not succeeded in locating and breaking up the underground network as yet. In Communist plans and calculations they have anticipated the removal of their united front organisers. These are the "expendables", the men who pay the price of detention in the hope that the Communist revolution may eventually triumph. Any man who is really valuable to the Communists and is not yet known to security intelligence, is never put to work in the open to run the risk of detention.

    Mr Speaker, Sir, the second reason why the threat is there is that the united front framework is left intact. They have arranged the temporary withdrawal of their reserve team in the united front. A number of these men cannot immediately be traced. After some time, they will come out and carry on where the first team left off. And the underground leaders can always throw in a few more trained cadres to help the reserve team reactivate and revitalise the united front, particularly at the time of elections after election writs have been issued. Members will remember that in several major pronouncements after the referendum last year, when they knew that they had decisively lost in the fight against merger and Malaysia, Mr Lim Ching Siong warned of the difficult struggle ahead and of the need to conserve their strength and

Column: 394

carry on the struggle. Well, they have done exactly this.

    A considerable number of the leaders involved in the Communist united front are men who have come from the Federation. Because of conditions during the Emergency in the Federation and because of the sterner measures there taken against the Communists, some of their best Communist cadres have come to Singapore. One of our problems is that not only do we have our own share of Communist cadres, but that we also have in our small island a considerable number of Federation Communist cadres. This time some 20 of them, key organisers, all of Federation origin, have been ordered by the I.S.C. to be sent hack to the Federation; and there they will remain. They will not be allowed to return to Singapore to frequent their old haunts and cause trouble again.

    All those detained and those still not detained engaged in the conspiracy should remember that it is up to them to decide if they want a decent place in our society. If they give up this dangerous nonsense of revolution for a Communist Malaya, and now a Communist Malaysia, and stop taking their directives from foreign groups, they can be released immediately. We have no desire to keep anybody out of a fair share of the fruits of our society, whether Chinese-educated, Malay-educated, Tamil-educated, or English-educated. Everybody can share in the fruits of freedom and join in the building of our nation.

    But let me remind those who are still determined on violent revolution and the setting up of a Communist society, that this time they face nationalism, a much more formidable and enduring opponent than colonialism. Colonialism, Mr Speaker, Sir, is on the way out. Nationalism will stay and triumph.

    The Barisan Sosialis bore the brunt of the onslaught and has suffered the most casualties. From our Central Executive Committee alone, nine members have been arrested and detained. Koh Thong, Fong Swee Suan, Dr Lim Hock Siew, Lim Shee Ping, Dominic Puthucheary and Tan Yam Seng. From our Central Cultural sub-committee, Central Organisation sub-committee, Publication sub-committee and Branch Committees, altogether more than 40 from the Barisan Sosialis have been detained. I will table a list of names of Barisan members recently detained. The total number under detention, together with those from other organisations, we now learn, is 133. Nine have been released, leaving 124 still under detention. 124 innocent persons, deprived of their individual freedom and kept behind walls in solitary confinement, and given treatment worse than that of convicted criminals. Why? All because they oppose imperialism and neo-colonialism. All because they oppose the British-sponsored Malaysia, and because they, oppose the P.A.P. The powers that be, in order to give an excuse for locking them up, made them out to be dangerous men. The Prime Minister says, "These are the people who will mount the barricades." Yet, not so very long ago, he used to ridicule them as beer-hall revolutionaries. Now, because 4 suits the purpose of the P.A.P., they have suddenly become dangerous men. And, of course, it suits the Prime Minister. But let us ask: Did they steal or rob? No. Did they kill or murder? No. Did they take part in riots? No. Did they take up arms against the Government? Again, no! Yet, all these 124 persons have been arbitrarily arrested and detained without charge or trial, and treated worse than convicted criminals! Why? Why, Mr Prime Minister? Why, Mr Deputy Prime Minister?

    Today, as a result of the arrests, threats and intimidations a change has come over Singapore. The people prefer not to talk so very loudly of politics these days. Many clam up on politics the moment they see strangers around. There is an atmosphere of suspicion, uncertainty and fear. authority can resort to arbitrary arrests at any time. The only law in the State seems to be the law of the Police, the Special Branch and the P.A.P.

It was decided by us to send Lim Shee Ping as our delegate. He left Singapore on Friday, 1st February, 1963, and was on his way to Moshi when his Federation passport was withdrawn at Nairobi. The Straits Tunes of the 4th February, 1963, says:

    `Authoritative sources disclosed tonight that he was intercepted at Nairobi, Kenya, on his way to Dar-es-Salaam. There the British authorities withdrew his Federation passport...'

    Let me emphasise, Sir. The British authorities withdrew his Federation passport at the request of the Federation Government. He was then put on a plane hound for Malaya. It is not that he went voluntarily by himself. But he was bodily put on a plane bound for Malaya.

Column: 404



    "It is not known when he left Nairobi and whether he will be flown back to Singapore or Kuala Lumpur." This is the high-handed action of arbitrary arrest carried out across the high seas and across international boundaries. And for what reason? Did he commit murder or some serious international crime that needed the services of Interpol? Lim Shee Ping committed no crime. He had been seen off only the day before at the Airport by many of us, and he was then on his way to an International Conference. Yet he was arbitrarily stopped, arrested and sent back to Malaya! A cable was received from him informing us that his passport had been withdrawn and that he expected to arrive back in Singapore at 12 midnight on Monday. 4th February, 1963. We made several attempts to meet him, but of course they were all to no avail. The truth of the matter is - and here I challenge the Minister for Home Affairs in his answer to me only yesterday - Lim Shee Ping was secretly transferred en route in Bombay, or at Calcutta, from a Qantas flight to an Air India flight. If, according to the Minister for Home Affairs, he came back just because he did not have his passport, the authorities would not have transferred him from one flight to another. And instead of arriving back in Singapore at 12 midnight as expected or on an earlier Qantas flight at 7 p.m. he arrived back in Singapore at 5 p.m instead. Instead of 12 midnight or instead of a bit earlier at 7 o'clock, he arrived back at 5 o'clock. This was specially arranged by the British authorities to ensure that we would not have a chance of meeting him. Newspapers next morning headlined, "In and out and nobody knew". "Detainee Lim expected on one plane . . . He came by another." This is the Machiavellian plotting of pro-colonial stooges and agents in order to deprive people of their freedom.

since the arrests. There is now no freedom of association and assembly. On top of all this, we are now denied the freedom of publication.

Our printers had their licences suspended and they were forced to go out of business for ten days.     Sir, there are a number of allegations in the Internal Security Council's statement issued after the arrests on 2nd February, chief among which are:

    (1) that the Barisan Sosialis and other organisations are under control of the Communists;

    (2) that the three Governments concur in the arrests: (this, according to the Prime Minister, is the wisdom of the P.A.P. Ministers)

    (4) that they were arrested because of their open support of the uprising in Brunei and their resorting to violence and bloodshed.

    Sir, let us examine these allegations one by one, as well as other points in the Internal Security Council's statement and see whether they are justifiable allegations. Let us first deal with the subject of Communism.

    Communism is the pet subject of the Prime Minister and is an accusation that is always raised by the colonialists to justify every repression against anti-colonial forces. Ever since the Second World War, and even before that, national liberation movements, which the Prime Minister nowadays speaks so slightingly of, in all colonial countries have been daily gaining in momentum, and colonial powers have always used this accusation to deny the people their legitimate rights and aspirations in the colonies and semi-colonies in Asia, Africa and Latin America. The Communist bogey has always been used to frighten and intimidate the people. Almost all nationalist leaders in countries that have now gained their independence had at one time or another been accused of being Communists, pro-Communists or Communist-front men. This has, however, not prevented their helping in the liberation of their own countries from the yoke of foreign domination, nor the inevitable collapse of colonialism. Many were imprisoned for their beliefs and for the part they played in their just national struggles. But, in almost every case, the colonial powers had been compelled ultimately by pressure of public opinion and the inevitable march of history to release them and to recognise them as true national leaders of their countries.

    In our country, all anti-colonial stalwarts, all who wage an uncompromising struggle against imperialism and colonialism, and all true patriots, have at one time or another been labelled Communists of one hue or another. Even Lee Kuan Yew, the McCarthy type anti-Communist of today, and ironically the self-professed Communist collaborator

Column: 410

of yesterday, was at one time also labelled Communist. He was then wearing the mask of anti-colonialism and he was pretending to fight against imperialism and colonialism. Of course, he is now completely unmasked. He is now exposed through and through - he is now seen in his true colours - an out-and-out colonial stooge, a running dog of the imperialists.

    Sir, this charge of Communism is not new. In fact, so long as colonialism in whatever shape or form exists, and so long as we struggle against colonialism, so long will this charge of Communism hang over us.

    This business of the Communist conspiracy is so widespread that it haunts even the countries of the sovereign powers themselves. I was informed by a British Member of Parliament, Mr William Warbey, when I was in London recently that the stories of the Communist conspiracy in Singapore reminded him very much of the stories put out before the war by the British Government in Britain itself. Thus, one can see that this Communist bogey is something that is not confined to the colonial territories alone. It is also present in the very heartland of the colonial power itself. In fact, it is present wherever privileged groups exist and when they try to prolong their oppression and exploitation of the people. It is especially used by Fascist dictators and tyrannical oppressors who find in the Communist bogey an excuse for all sorts of repressive actions and terror. Hitler made use of this bogey, and we know today what the world thinks of him.

    In British territories the world over today, wherever there is a national liberation movement or some strong Opposition to colonial rule there is this Communist label bandied around. So, in Malaya, when the Federation politicians and the Prime Minister make this same accusation, they are merely echoing the words of British colonialism in many parts of the world. Indeed, they are merely joining the chorus of men like Chiang Kai-shek, Syngman Rhee and Ngo Dinh Diem - Fascist dictators who use anti-Communism as an excuse for all

Column: 411

sorts of repressions. We have already seen the Minister for Education making friends with Ngo Dinh Diem, a person whom the Prime Minister used to condemn not so very long ago.

    We must remember, when we talk of Communism, that the M.C.P. has been an illegal organisation for the last 15 years, and every effort has been made by the police and colonial troops to hunt down every Communist. It is convenient to label all strong opposition as Communists, as it paves the way for the colonial power to invoke the law against such opposition. But what is the result of such Communist-labelling? It does Snot solve the problems of poverty. It only results in the crippling of all democratic forms Of expression that exist. Already we see the Communist label being used in Singapore to deny workers and trade unions their fundamental rights of freedom of association and assembly. Even political Parties have been similarly denied their freedom of assembly. I do not need to mention the banning of the ten publications and journals of political Parties, trade Unions, universities and other organisations. Those who wish to oppose Malaysia constitutionally, like our comrades and friends in the Barisan Sosialis and other political Parties, trade unions and civic organisations, have been arbitrarily arrested and detained. This Government simply hangs the Communist label on them. This label of Communism is, with few exceptions, only applied to persons of Chinese origin. The Party Rakyat and the people of Brunei revolted against the imposition of Malaysia, but being mostly of the Malay race, the charge of Communism is not levelled at them. Of course, this is only an example Of the colonial policy of divide and rule. The colonialists hope to fan the flames of inter-communal suspicion and discord.     Sir, the opposition to Malaysia has a genuine basis and has nothing to do with any Communist plot, indeed, this opposition is because of the imperialist plot. Instead of answering the injustices of the Malaysia Plan, the British, Federation and Singapore Governments run away from answering by calling us Communists and by putting leaders, who oppose Malaysia, in prison. They cannot answer our proof that Malaysia is unacceptable to the majority of the people. Their answer is the answer of Fascist dictators - arrest, imprisonment and torture. By crying Communism, of course, they hope to side-track the attention of the people from their oppression and exploitation and to confuse them. By arresting the leaders, they hope also to intimidate the people into abjectly accepting Malaysia and to prevent further opposition to the Malaysia Plan. As I have said, they want to create the impression to the outside world that there is very little opposition to Malaysia, and that the majority support Malaysia.     Let me touch a little on why the P.A.P. is so fond of this Communist line. Why is the P.A.P. so fond of the Communist bogey? The Prime Minister delights in talking about Communism. He enjoys talking Communism and for very good reasons too. Why? Let us analyse why. The Prime Minister and his opportunistic friends like the Communist line. Why? Because with this Communist bogey, they hope to deceive the people and frighten them. I have already mentioned that. They hope to use the Communist bogey as a tool by which to crush political opposition and if political opposition could be crushed, then, of course, there would be no great difficulty in their maintaining themselves in office.

    The Barisan Sosialis today offers the greatest effective opposition to the P.A.P. Therefore, the first objective of the P.A.P. is to identify the Barisan Sosialis with the Communist bogey, and through the excuse and pretext of dealing with the Communists, the P.A.P. hope to hit at the Barisan Sosialis and all other organisations that offer effective Opposition to the P.A.P. That is reason No. 1.

    The second reason is the Prime Minister uses the omnipresent Communist as a ready-made scapegoat for all the sins of commission and omission of the P.A.P. Thus blames the Communist for all the P.A.P. mistakes and failures, for all the P.A.P. broken promises, for all the P.A.P. undemocratic and Fascist repressive actions, for all P.A.P. reactionary and pro-colonial policies. In fact, everything that goes wrong is indiscriminately blamed on the omni-present Communist.

    The third reason is this. It follows from this that since all mistakes and faults are laid at the door-step of the Communist bogey, the Prime Minister and his P.A.P. Ministers can claim themselves to be always right, to be always infallible. They then hope to absolve

Column: 414

themselves from all blame under all circumstances, and on all big vital issues that have aroused the indignation of the people.

    The fourth reason is this. The Prime Minister also uses this Communist bogey with the hope of silencing opposition to P.A.P. undemocratic and Fascist ways. As the M.C.P. is an illegal body in Singapore and the Federation, no one will be able to speak up in public on its behalf without at the same time being smeared as Communist or pro-Communist. Thus the Prime Minister hopes to silence even the uncommitted into not daring to openly and publicly oppose or criticise P.A.P. leaders. With luck, the Prime Minister also hopes even to intimidate them into "supporting" the P.A.P.

    Reason No. 5 is this. With this Communist bogey, the P.A.P. hopes also to alienate certain sections of the people from us in the Barisan Sosialis and thus restrict and limit the growing strength and influence of the Barisan Sosialis. Thus, from the very beginning, since our break with the P.A.P., we in the Barisan Sosialis have been labelled Communist and pro-Communist, and the Barisan Sosialis and other anti-P.A.P. organisations have been labelled Communist front organisations, and so on.

    The 12 radio talks and the publication of thousands and thousands of The Battle For Merger booklets were all designed to scare and frighten people away from us in the Barisan Sosialis. Thus, the Communist bogey becomes the useful tool by which P.A.P. leaders hope to crush political opposition.

    Sir, since the Emergency in June 1948, repressive laws have turned our country into a police state. When the Emergency Regulations were withdrawn in Singapore in 1955, they were replaced by the P.P.S.O. and under the P.P.S.O., large numbers of our patriots and anti-colonial stalwarts have been arrested and detained without trial. Many are still languishing in prison after seven years without charge or trial, detained at the pleasure of the colonial masters.

    The Universal Declaration of Human Rights, Articles 18 and 19 have this to say. This is the 1945 United Nations Universal Declaration of Human Rights. Article 18 says:

    `Everyone has the right to freedom of thought, conscience and religion. The right includes freedom to change his religion or belief and freedom either alone or in company with others in public or private to manifest his religion or belief in teaching, practice, worship and observance.'

    Article 19 says:

    `Everyone has the right to freedom of opinion and expression. This right includes freedom to hold opinions without interference and to seek, receive and impart information and ideas through any media and regardless of frontiers.'

This is our Universal Declaration of Human Rights, Articles 18 and 19. But what do we find in Singapore, the Borneo territories and the Federation? It is entirely different from the recognised United Nations Universal Declaration of Human Rights. The Constitution lays it down that there is freedom of speech and publication, association and assembly. But it is not the rights that exist on paper that count. It is whether or not these rights can be exercised and enforced in practice that really counts. Voltaire many years ago said:

    `I detest your views. But I am prepared to die for your right to express them.'

Can the Prime Minister and his Ministers rise to just one-hundredth of the stature of Voltaire?

    Today to deny these rights to the people, subterfuges and cover-up charges are laid at the door-steps of the people. And under the pretext of safeguarding the "security of the state," repressive action has been extensively carried out! The mere fact that these
