allegations are made and no charge and trial is given shows the hollowness of the allegations.

    What is the Special Branch? I had worked in the Ministry of Home Affairs for a short period and I have come to learn a number of detestable things about the Special Branch. We all know that the Special Branch in Singapore is merely an off-shoot of the secret police started in the middle of the 19th century in England itself. Spies and agents were employed by the Government at the time when the struggle between the capitalists and the workers were assuming significant proportions. And these spies and agents were employed to deal with the working class in the land of the very heart of imperialism itself. This secret police very rapidly expanded its influence all-pervadingly to all the government departments, not only in the United Kingdom, but very quickly also to the colonies. Its powers are extensive. Even Parliament and our Assembly have no say in the running of the secret police, and I dare say even the Ministers, more often than not, know nothing of what is happening inside the Special Branch in Robinson Road, Singapore, to say nothing of Assemblymen, Backbenchers and other people.

    I learned the other day, when one of the Ministers was asked why there should be arrests this time, that he said he knew nothing of what was happening. He did not know a single thing and yet he is a Minister of the Government today! This merely proves my point, Sir, that even Ministers do not know what is happening in Robinson Road Special Branch.

    The Special Branch is there to serve not the interests of the people of Singapore but the interests of colonialism and imperialism. The Special Branch is directly linked with the United Kingdom Commissioner in Singapore and the big-wigs of the British Military Forces who are here not to serve the interests of the people of Singapore, but to serve the interests of people outside Singapore. They are here, not to give us freedom, but to oppress and to deny the people of Singapore their legitimate hopes and aspirations. The wide powers of arrests

Column: 419

and detention given to the Special Branch under the P.P.S.O. surprised even the people of the United Kingdom itself. There in the United Kingdom, the powers of the secret police are strictly limited by the safeguards in the habeas corpus. This is not possible in Singapore today under the P.P.S.O. And from this alone, Sir, we should be able to see what a repressive instrument the P.P.S.O. is today in Singapore.

    Today, the Special Branch, being merely a colonial organ of repression, maligns all anti-colonial political Parties, organisations and progressive individuals as Communists and those who oppose the P.A.P. are, of course, automatically Communists. The Prime Minister tells us there are only 300 Communists in Singapore. But because hundreds of thousands in political Parties, trade unions and civic organisations oppose the P.A.P., these hundreds of thousands have all suddenly become Communists. The Prime Minister used to ridicule them and called them all sorts of fancy names. They were all beer-hall revolutionaries, arm-chair revolutionaries and what-not. But because he fears their opposition today, he has arbitrarily arrested them, detained them. Now he has a chance to pose to the people again, not as an anti-colonialist, but as an oppressor of the people of Singapore.

    Dr Lee Siew Choh: --- and there are Special Branch officers who are permanently stuck to coffee shops, and just do not budge. Some of them, of course, do it very openly. The very nature of spying itself requires that they keep on lying. They spy and lie all the time. An undercover agent has to deceive associates into thinking him to be one of themselves. And the longer the spies and informers are at their jobs the greater is the blurring of the thin line between truth and falsehood. These spies, in order to gain the good favours of their superiors, very, very often have great imagination. The imagination turns to beautiful embroidery and fabrication of events that did not take place and of words that were never said. Moreover, there is no possibility of verifying the reports of spies and informers. The mistakes of doctors and accountants can be checked, but the only witness to so-called conspiracy is the victim the spy wants to punish. Under those circumstances, how can we ever believe the words of these spies and informers the weight of whose information the P.A.P. Government depends on so heavily?

The answer is simple, it is obvious that none of the three alone would like to face the music of (he wrath of the people. But let us first find out why the British and the Federation Governments want to take repressive action. The British are cunning and experienced colonialists. They have been at the game for hundreds of years and from past experience they know that repressive action of any sort will only engender resentment and bitter hatred among the people. If the British alone were to take any repressive action, they alone would become the object of opprobrium and hatred of the people, They would therefore prefer that repressive action be taken by stooges, if possible. It would take away the sharp edge of criticism of world opinion against them. The stooges would then have to share and even take the brunt of resentment and hatred that such repressive action would cause. Moreover, it would allow the British to present themselves still as democrats. And if embarrassing questions are asked in the British Parliament, for instance, they could pass the buck on to the local Government and their stooges, and let them fend for themselves. It is not

the British that has to sell the idea of Malaysia, but their No. 1 salesman - the Lee Kuan Yew clique - that travels all round the world hoping to deceive other countries about Malaysia. It is Lee Kuan Yew and Company and not the British who are the most vociferous and demonstrative in the propaganda promotion and defence of Malaysia. It is the P.A.P. that had to rig the referendum and not the British, though with British connivance, in order to give a false and distorted impression of the wishes of the people of Singapore to the outside world. And inflated indeed was the Prime Minister with artificial colonial pomp and prestige. He was showered with praise from the colonial master.

    Finally today the ridiculous position in which the P.A.P. has found itself has caused it to take repressive action against the people of Singapore, a treachery which will condemn the P.A.P. for generations to come.

    The British lion indeed has very seductively and cunningly manoeuvred the P.A.P into a situation where the P.A.P. willy-nilly becomes the handmaid and errand boy of British imperialism. The British want to protect and preserve their interests so that they may continue to exploit the resources in the region: and this they have apparently temporarily succeeded in so doing, thanks to the mass arrests. Thanks to the collaboration of their minions and stooges in the P.A P.

    For the British, therefore, to concur with the repressive action on 2nd February, 1963, or at any time for that matter, is not difficult to understand. The history of the United Kingdom and the history of the British Empire abound with such repressive actions. Pick up any history book, even a British one, and we see repression and oppression written on every page - repression which they have euphemistically called "the glory of Empire building".

    Now, what of the Federation Government? The Federation Government is a Right-wing, feudalistic Government. It represents the interests of the feudalists, the Right-wing reactionary compradores and the privileged few. The

Column: 425

U.M.N.O. Alliance, catering for opportunists, communalists and political careerists, have long been schooled and nurtured by the British as their faithful ally, collaborator and agent, so that they may continue to look after British interests. In so doing, they of course look after their own interests as well, the privileged and the selected few. The interests of the vast majority of the people - of the workers, farmers and fishermen - are but of secondary importance to them.

    The reactionary Government in the Federation fears the growing strength of the socialist forces and, dominated by the communal and sectional interests, it has already from time to time made arrests of anti-colonial forces to prevent them from reaching and enlightening the masses in the rural areas. The Alliance would prefer to benumb the masses with communal propaganda and prevent them from knowing the real causes and root of their poverty.

    The situation in Singapore is different compared to that in the Federation. Here the masses through years of anti-colonial struggle have gained a better insight into the workings of colonial propaganda. They know that their interests coincide with the interests of the working class as a whole and, with the guidance and leadership of a strong Left-wing movement, they are daily marching forward with the advance of socialist forces.

    The Federation Government, being reactionary and feudalistic, therefore, fears a strong Left-wing movement in Singapore. Communally-inspired politicians in the Federation fear that the influence of Left-wing forces will extend to the Federation. They fear that Singapore will become a "Cuba", as the Prime Minister says, and just as President Kennedy wants to remove the so-called subversion of Cuba, so the Federation politicians today want to contain and control and, if possible, completely suppress the Left-wing movement in Singapore.

    Mr Emmanuel Pelaez, Vice-President of the Philippines, had said in London that they were given to understand that

Column: 426

the primary purpose of the proposed Federation of Malaysia is, as it were, to "sterilise" Singapore as a centre of so-called Communist influence. In addition, should Malaysia really be imposed on the people against their will through the use of brute force and in complete disregard of the danger signals, the Left-wing forces in Singapore could still become a constant headache, to say the least, to whatever Grand Alliance the Tunku and pro-Malaysia forces may be able to form in Malaya and in the Borneo territories.

    Under the circumstances, the Federation most certainly would like to remove all strong opposition in Singapore whenever possible. So the Federation's concurrence with the arrests on 2nd February is also not unexpected. The British agree to the arrests and the Federation agrees to the arrests; and what does the P.A.P. do? Being stooges and lackeys of the British, the P.A.P. has to listen to its master's voice and carry out its master's instructions. Moreover, the P.A.P. has its own selfish reasons for joining the British and the Federation Governments in their dirty work. I will come to more of this by and by.

    But fearful of repercussions following the arrests and hoping to confuse public opinion and hoping to deceive a section of the people, the P.A.P. comes out with those high-sounding words, "security of the State". And according to the Prime Minister, repressive actions had to be taken and mass arrests carried out on 2nd February because the so-called Communist front men in the Barisan Sosialis constitute a danger to the security of Singapore and to the other territories that go to form Malaysia.

    The reason which the Straits Times, the mouthpiece of the colonialists and the imperialists, praised so forcefully that its editorial on the 4th of February states:-

    `Justification for their arrests could hardly be argued more powerfully than that.'

"More powerfully than that". What a pat on the back for the P.A.P. - and from the mouthpiece of the colonial master

Column: 427

too - like the pat on the back of a dog from its master! But let us take a look at the so-called powerful argument and see what the argument really amounts to. "A danger to the security of Singapore" - such a high-sounding justification for the arrests. But under the cloak of these four magical words, "security of the State", all the sins in the world have been committed throughout the ages. On the excuse to safeguard the security of the State, the most blatant cases of imperialist aggression, exploitation and enslavement of countless weaker nations have been perpetrated and so-called "justified".

    To safeguard the security of the State, the tyrants and Fascist dictators have resorted to repressive actions at home and abroad: at home, to preserve the privileges of the tyrannical ruling class; and abroad, to exploit and oppress other weaker and less developed nations. For the security of the State, demands of the people for urgent reforms have been rejected out of hand, and their legitimate rights and aspirations denied and suppressed. In the name of the security of the State, the most fundamental rights of man have been violated, justice denied, democracy trampled underfoot. Under the cloak of this high-sounding phrase, the four magical words "security of the State", millions and millions of people have been tortured and enslaved, oppressed and exploited. Under the cloak of the security of the State, the foreign master rules over an unwilling subject people with an iron hand, and they are not even given a chance to determine their own future.

    Sir, history abounds with lurid examples of the grave abuse of these four simple words in every country, in every epoch, and in every age. Thus, to safeguard the security of the State, Hitler unleashed the world war on the people and had millions of Jews murdered. Similarly, to safeguard the security of the State, South Africa today practises apartheid, racial segregation and discrimination, and denies the true sons of the soil of their most basic and fundamental human rights.

Column: 428



    A few years go, to safeguard the security of the State, Eden ordered the invasion of the Suez Canal and the United Arab Republic.

    Dr Goh Keng Swee: What about Budapest?

    Dr Lee Siew Choh: And only a few months ago, to safeguard the security of the State, Kennedy threatened to invade Cuba and bring about a nuclear destruction of the world.

    Dr Goh Keng Swee: Stalin?

    Dr Lee Siew Choh: Do we need more examples? Nearer home, we see, Sir, in South Vietnam ---

    Dr Goh Keng Swee: Stalin?

    Dr Lee Siew Choh: --- under the cloak of the security of the State, democracy being trampled under-foot with millions of people subjected to the most humiliating tortures and denied the most fundamental of human rights. In Malaya and the whole of South-East Asia during the war. Japanese Fascist warlords committed the most brutal atrocities, again under the cloak of the security of the State. In our own Singapore, on the same excuse of safeguarding the security of the State, the most repressive actions had been perpetrated by the colonial forces and mercenary troops against the people of Singapore, with the loss of many innocent lives.

    Tun Lim Yew Hock Government followed the path of the colonial master and similarly gave the same trite excuse in the 1956 and 1957 purges, and was roundly condemned by the people of Singapore. Indeed the Prime Minister himself was one of those who most roundly condemned the Lim Yew Hock repression. Now, of course, the Prime Minister sings a different tune. Since 2nd February, the Lee Kuan Yew Government has been treading the same desperate path. Even the Prime Minister is mouthing the same time-worn excuse, with the forlorn hope that, if it was repeated often enough, it might exonerate the P.A.P. from all blame and save the P.A.P. from the wrath and condemnation of the people.

Column: 429



    Since so much force is given to this trite phrase and since the persons now detained have been alleged to have constituted a danger to the security of Singapore, let us ask: what do the British, the Federation and the P.A.P. mean by these words?

    If they mean that the Barisan Sosialis and the other arrested persons constitute a danger to the security of the vested interests of the foreign overlord and colonial master, of foreign monopoly-capitalists and the privileged few, then we say it is true and correct. If they mean that the Barisan Sosialis and the arrested persons constitute a danger to the security of the capitalist system of oppression and exploitation and to the security of the forces of reaction and repression and tyranny, then, again we say it is true and correct. If they mean that the Barisan Sosialis and the arrested persons constitute a danger to the system of discrimination, inequality, injustice, Fascism and enslavement, then again we say it is true and correct.

    The Barisan Sosialis, Sir, is pledged to eradicate colonialism and foreign domination from whatever source. We pledge ourselves to removing the capitalist system of oppression and exploitation. We dedicate ourselves to the struggle against the system of discrimination, inequality, injustice, Fascism, and enslavement. And we are proud of all this. We feel elated that we have constituted a danger to the security of all the hindrances and obstructions to progress and to the forward development of society. We want to get rid of all these hindrances and obstructions.

    Mr Rajaratnam: All words.

    Dr Lee Siew Choh: But if they mean that the Barisan Sosialis and the arrested persons constitute a danger to the basic interests of the workers, peasants, fishermen, intellectuals, and national businessmen, then we emphatically say it is not true. And if they mean we constitute a danger to the oppressed, the exploited, the enslaved, the under-privileged, the down-trodden and dispossessed, then again we emphatically say it is not true.

Column: 430

We in the Barisan Sosialis dedicate ourselves to the struggle for the fundamental rights of man, namely, justice, equality, democracy, freedom, and the right of self-determination.

We are pledged to the struggle to eradicate poverty, disease, ignorance and want. Are these really justifiable reasons for taking repressive action against the people? No. A thousand times no.

    Today because the colonialists want to retain the vested interests and deprive the people of their legitimate rights and aspirations, they have not hesitated to resort to arrests and detentions of anti-colonial stalwarts in a desperate attempt to slow down and impede the advance of the movement for colonial freedom. But these are only their death throes before final destruction and elimination. This has been proved many times over in history. "Political detainees are and indeed should be regarded as an anomaly in a democratic society." So say Devan Nair and Jek Yuen Thong, both top brass of the P.A.P. From a P.A.P. admission, it is clear that repressive action should never have been taken. If repressive action must be taken, let it be taken against those who wax rich through the exploitation and oppression of others, and those who continue to help impose foreign rule over us in Malaya.

    To stress on the three Governments concurring in the arrests does not add any weight to the argument. It can show how closely allied is the P.A.P. to reaction, feudalism, colonialism and imperialism. But it adds nothing to the strength of their arguments.

    I do not need to go into the shameful episode of the P.A.P. trying to pass the buck to the British and the Federation for the arrests. Knowing how abhorrent such repressive action is the P.A.P. leaders do not even have the guts to stand up to so-called "justify" - the unjustifiable arrests. The verdict of the people indeed is a terrible thing. It frightens the insides of the P.A.P. Ministers.

    Sir, we in the Barisan Sosialis have too often been accused of being anti-national. And because of the P.A.P. control of the radio, Rediffusion and the Press, the voice of the Barisan Sosialis has not been easily heard. Just what is meant by being a nationalist? When we talk of a person being a nationalist, we mean that he places national interests above sectional and personal interests. On the other hand, if a person places sectional and personal interests above national interests, then he becomes anti-national.

    Personal interests are interests of the individual; for example, the personal ambitions of power and wealth of P.A.P. Ministers. Sectional interests are interests of small groups of people, for example, the vested interests of foreign monopoly-capitalists and of the compradores and feudalists. But what are national interests? National interests are the basic interests of the country and of its people. They are the interests of the vast majority of the people. And these interests are the interests of the toiling masses - the workers, peasants, hawkers, shop assistants, intellectuals, small businessmen and national businessmen.

    We have been under colonial rule for 150 years. We are still under the heel of foreign domination. The country's

Column: 435

wealth has been taken away to enrich the colonialists and the imperialists. And we are still being oppressed and exploited.

    A true nationalist, therefore, is he who looks after the interests of the exploited and oppressed, and he who fights to eradicate colonialism and imperialism. A nationalist is he who struggles to strengthen the unity of the people, without distinction of race, colour or creed, to rid our country of foreign domination. A nationalist is he who struggles to improve the livelihood of the toiling masses.

    He who helps the colonialists and the imperialists to enslave the people is anti-national. He who seeks to destroy the unity of the people by playing on their communal fears is anti-national. He who collaborates with the foreigners and the colonialists, and promotes colonial schemes to enslave the people is anti-national. And he who helps to keep foreign troops on our soil to suppress the legitimate aspirations of the people is anti-national.

    Of course, some politicians try to equate personal and sectional interests with national interests. In this way, opportunities, like those in the P.A.P., would then call themselves nationalists in order to confuse and deceive the people.

    Let us now ask the Prime Minister and his other Ministers a few simple questions. Who is collaborating with the colonialists today? Who is the errand boy of the imperialists today? Who is promoting the British-sponsored Malaysia today? Who is selling our country to a foreign power today? Who is collaborating to subjugate the peoples of the Federation, Singapore, Sarawak, Brunei and Sabah under colonial domination and denying them their fundamental rights of self-determination and independence? Who wants to keep foreign troops on our soil for the suppression of the legitimate aspirations of the people? And who is trying to justify the use of the British bases for the suppression of the national liberation struggle in Kalimantan Utara? The answer is

Column: 436

clear to all in Singapore. It is none other than the Prime Minister and his traitorous clique. It is the P.A.P. that is collaborating with the foreign powers. It is the P.A.P. that is running errands for the imperialists. It is the P.A.P. that is promoting British-sponsored Malaysia. It is the P.A.P. that is collaborating to subjugate the peoples of the Federation, Singapore, Sarawak, Brunei and Sabah under colonial domination. It is the P.A.P. that is denying them their fundamental rights of self-determination and independence. And it is the P.A.P. again that wants to keep foreign troops on our soil for the suppression of the legitimate aspirations of our peoples.

    The anti-colonial elements are, therefore, as can be seen from my arguments, in the P.A.P. We here and now charge the P.A.P. as the anti-nationalist elements of our country, collaborating with foreign colonialists to control and dominate our country at the expense of our people! The P.A.P. clique are the out-and-out anti-nationals, the traitors who have sold the rights of our people - the workers, peasants, hawkers, taxi-drivers and students - down the drain! Yes, the P.A.P., the anti-national traitors masquerading as nationalists. That answers this anti-nationalist allegation of the P.A.P.

occurs to depart from constitutional methods and to jeopardise national defence and Singapore's security by joining with groups resorting to violence and blood-shed as in the Borneo Territories.'

A little while back the Prime Minister also talked of the meeting in Nee Soon and people travelling in Car SR. 5222. What is wrong with people travelling in cars?; what is wrong with people going about? What is all this that they are trying to bring out? Sir, I have always thought that the Prime Minister had some originality in him when he talked about the "Plen" and things like that. Owing to the tardiness of their communications, it was not until the 1st January, 1944, that this man reached our camp at Blantar. Prime Minister has been doing? This book says here in the first page, even before you start reading the story: "This book is copyright.     Sir, as leaders of political Parties with common objectives, like our common opposition to neo-colonial Malaysia, and being co-members of the same socialist conference, from which the P.A.P. was ejected, it is only natural and normal that they should meet frequently and whenever the opportunity occurs, for the exchange of views and opinions about political developments, as well as for the promotion and strengthening of friendly co-operation and friendly ties.

Even the colonial mouthpiece, the Straits Times, said so. Azahari attended our inaugural meeting

and spoke at the rally in the Happy World Stadium in September 1961. Such meetings take place in the normal course of events. On the contrary, it would indeed be unusual and abnormal if there were no such meetings. For obvious reasons, the P.A.P. and the Straits Times have now gone out of their way to paint innocent, open and normal events with loud and lurid colours. Even the Straits Times again admitted so in their editorial of 4th February, 1963. Azahari had been in the Barisan Sosialis' headquarters on several occasions and many of us had met him and talked to him. All in order to create the impression of some super front page conspiracy very luckily and

Column: 440

very timely discovered, of course, by the sharp prying eyes of the Prime Minister and the Special Branch. But for which a major catastrophe would have befallen the people of Singapore! Such is the fairy tale of the British lion and the P.A.P. dog - the running dog!

But in spite of all the efforts of the Straits Times to spotlight this so-called "link" and this so-called "conspiracy", the people of - Singapore still cannot understand why the arrests were necessary. Even the Straits Times editorial of 4th February, 163, complained that the Government case was weak and unconvincing. The Straits Times editorial of 4th February states:

    `The statement issued by the Internal Security council has little in it that has not been hashed and rehashed in the newspaper for months past, except perhaps for the dealings which Azahari had with Barisan Sosialis leaders and even these contacts were an open secret.'

    The editorial went on to hope for the publication of

"the full [I am reading from a few lines above what I have just quoted] or at least a fuller story of the circumstances which forced the I.S.C. to take strong measures before it was too late."

    In other words, even the Straits Times admitted that there was no justification in fact for the arrests! Yes, there was no justifiable excuse whatsoever for the arrests. What are the circumstances which, according to the Straits Times, "forced the I.S.C. to take strong measure before it was too late"? Was it because we held a rally in support of the Brunei uprising?

    True, we held a rally in Tanjong Katong Road two weeks after the uprising in support of the Brunei National Liberation Movement. We applied for permission for the rally, clearly stating the reason for the rally in the application for the permits, and the permit was granted for a rally clearly staged to support the national uprising in Brunei. So it was all open and lawful. The Government had given us lawful permission to hold a rally in support of Brunei.

Column: 441

So obviously there was nothing wrong with the lawful rally for which a permit was issued by the P.A.P. Government. We have not taken up arms against the Government. We merely held a rally to voice our support in a legitimate democratic manner for an anti-colonial struggle in Brunei. Just as the P.A.P. and the Alliance Government had voiced their support for the anti-colonial struggle in Algeria only two years ago. On that occasion a rally was held in front of the Padang in which even the employers were specifically told to let workers get off earlier so that they could go to listen to Dr Ferhat Abbas and the Prime Minister. In that mass rally, the Prime Minister had spoken with staged feelings and had exhorted the people of Singapore to learn from the anti-colonial struggle of the Algerian people against the French imperialists. Of course, the Prime Minister then was only trying to deceive the people.

    Then, if you will remember, Sir, in this very House a few weeks later the Government went a stage further and moved a motion to contribute $10,000 to the Algerian fund as a token of sympathy and support and asked the House to record its admiration for the determination and courage of the Algerian people in their struggle for freedom against the tyranny and oppression of French colonialism; and on behalf of the people of Singapore expressed its wholehearted support for the cause of freedom for the Algerian people. In the ensuing debate all P.A.P. leaders spoke brave, inspiring words. Even Members of the Right-wing S.P.A. joined in the chorus. Let me refer you, Sir, to Hansard, Volume 14, No. 13 of 22nd February, 1961. May I refer you to column 1020? It is a pity the Minister for Culture is not here because he had spoken in paragraph 4 at column 1020 of "the rising tide of nationalism" and the "dyke of repression against the tidal wave of nationalist revolt, and how the dyke broke and colonialism was swept into the sea." Very inspiring words, Sir, and at that time I was taken in myself. I have mentioned paragraph 3. It was paragraph 4.

Column: 442



    Then in column 1021 on the next page, the third paragraph, somewhere in the middle, the Minister for Culture said:

    `Therefore, when confronted by the assertions of Algerian nationalism and Algerian demands for freedom, the French colons, backed by French generals, are trying to counter Algerian nationalism with repression and terror.

    It was French extremism which forced a moderate and conciliatory Algerian nationalism to resist French repression and violence with violence of its own.'.

Sir, these are words which nobody who calls himself an anti-colonialist can can quarrel with. And they are inspiring words. But let us just substitute the word "British" for the word "French" and the word "Brunei" for the word "Algeria", and the quote now reads as follows:

    `Therefore, when confronted by the assertions of Bruneian nationalism and Bruneian demands for freedom, the British colons, backed by British generals, are trying to counter Bruneian nationalism with repression and terror. It was British extremism which forced a moderate and conciliatory Bruneian nationalism to resist British repression and violence with violence of its own.'

It is a pity, Sir, that the Ministers do not listen to their own words because if they did they would see how ridiculous they have been in their accusations and allegations that we are supporting the Brunei uprising and resorting to violence and bloodshed.

    Then in column 1030 - this time the Deputy Prime Minister talked of the "mutual feelings of sympathy between the Provisional Government of the Algerian leaders and ourselves in Singapore because Singapore is still a colony, a semi-colony." Then he said in the second paragraph, near the end:

    `It is because of this understanding of peoples who have in the past been under colonial domination that we, the P.A.P. Government, have moved this motion in support of the Algerian people's struggle for independence against French imperialism.'

Again beautiful words, words which no anti-colonialist could disagree with. But, again, let us substitute the word "Brunei" for the word "Algeria" and

Column: 443

the word "British" for the word "French" and the meaning again is very clear. It would read:

    `It is because of this understanding of peoples who have in the past been under colonial domination that we, the P.A.P. Government, have moved this motion in support of the Brunei people's struggle for independence against British imperialism.'

    Let me go just a little further ---

    Mr Speaker: Order. May I suggest to the hon. Member that he is labouring on a point which he has already made. He has made the point. Can we proceed a little quicker with this debate?

    Dr Lee Siew Choh: I understand your impatience, Sir. Similarly, have I not wanted to stay up until this late hour ---

    Mr Speaker: Order. The complaint is not the late hour. The complaint is that the hon. Member is labouring a point which he has already made. And in a debate, once a Member, or once any debater has made a point, surely he should be satisfied and not labour the point.

    Dr Lee Siew Choh: Very well, Sir, I thought of just quoting the Member for Tanglin, but anyway, he is not here. However, I must quote the Prime Minister. In column 1032 the Prime Minister talks of the necessity to make a gesture in the forum of world debate to show what we think of the French imperialists. He says in column 1032:

    `But it is significant that in a world in which total war means total annihilation, the conflict is reduced to a secondary plane of a limited war with unlimited world support. There is pressure in the United Nations. There are expressions of sympathy and solidarity and we throw in our voice in support of the chorus on behalf of the freedom of the people of Algeria.'

All I need say, Sir, is to substitute the word "British" for "French" and the word "Brunei" for "Algeria" and we see that there is fundamentally no difference between the situation then and the situation today.

    If you will remember that debate, the Government finally asked the Assembly to pass a resolution which, if you were to leave out the second part of money contribution and if we substituted the

Column: 444

appropriate words to fit in with the context of our present situation, would read as follows:

    `That this Assembly records its admiration for the determination and courage of the Brunei people in the struggle for freedom against the tyranny and oppression of British colonialism and on behalf of the people of Singapore expresses its whole-hearted support for the cause for freedom for the Brunei people.'

Wholehearted support for the freedom for the Brunei people!

    Sir, our rally at Tanjong Katong held on the 23rd December, 1962, did not have the support of the Legislative Assembly, and we could not presume to speak on behalf of all the people of Singapore. But we did hold the rally to demonstrate our whole-hearted support for the people of Brunei openly and for all to see. It was not done furtively. In our rally we did exactly what the P.A.P. had previously done in another rally as well as officially in the Singapore Legislative Assembly on behalf of the people of Singapore.

    Today, we in the Barisan also admire the courage and determination of the people of Brunei' in their struggle for freedom against the tyranny and oppression of British colonialism. We in the Barisan call on the people to give whole-hearted support for the cause of freedom of the people in Brunei. Can it be that support for the cause of freedom against the French was correct and that against the British is wrong? Can it be that we must condemn French colonialism, but must love, admire and protect British colonialism? Is that what the P.A.P. want? If our support today for the Brunei people was wrong and unlawful, then similarly the P.A.P. and Assembly support in 1961 for the Algerian people was wrong and unlawful. If the admiration for the courage and determination of the Brunei people to be free was wrong and unlawful, then similarly the feigned P.A.P. admiration for the courage and determination of the Algerian people was wrong and unlawful. There cannot be two different standards of moral values. No one has suggested that feigned P.A.P. admiration for the courage and determination of the Algerian people to be free and feigned P.A.P. support of the Algerian struggle for freedom was wrong and unlawful.

Column: 445



    In fact, only a few months back, the P.A.P. took great pride in, and gave full publicity to, its past so-called support of the Algerian struggle. So how can anyone suggest that our support and admiration for the courage and determination of the Brunei people's struggle for freedom is wrong and unlawful? Or is it seriously suggested that what is done by the P.A.P. is right and lawful, but what is similarly done by other people becomes wrong and unlawful? Is there one law for the P.A.P. and another law for the rest of the people? Is that what is troubling us today in Singapore? Does being the Government make the P.A.P. right in everything the P.A.P. does? Does being the Government make all the difference between right and wrong, lawful and unlawful, loyalty and subversion?

    The Prime Minister himself had feigned support for anti-colonial struggles before, that is, until he had been unmasked as a mere opportunist and a stooge. But why this apparent turnabout, this volte-face. The I.S.C. statement goes on to say that "their open support for armed revolt in Brunei and their close connections with leaders of the revolt show that they are ready when the opportunity occurs to depart from constitutional methods and to jeopardise national defence and Singapore's security by joining with groups resorting to violence and blood-shed as in the Borneo territories."

    I have shown that the so-called "connection" and "link" are but fanciful concoctions of the fertile imagination of the colonialists and their stooges. The most unconnected events and happenings have been interlaced with "link" and "connections". The imagination is allowed to run riot. Everything is dominated by one obsession, namely, to prejudice public opinion against the persons whom the P.A.P. wants to fix and to destroy. We in the Barisan Sosialis want to struggle constitutionally for our political aims. But it has become increasingly difficult to continue the constitutional struggle. I have already said that door after door of the constitutional struggle has been slammed by the Fascist and arbitrary actions of the P.A.P., and the latest spate of arbitrary

Column: 446

arrests has forced the people to consider seriously whether or not all means of such constitutional struggle have been completely closed to the Opposition.

    Constitutional struggle, Sir, can only be undertaken when there are constitutional means left for the people to do so. At the present moment just when the Opposition has become strong enough to overthrow the Government through the democratic one-man-one-vote process, the powers-that-be have resorted to the most unconstitutional methods of arbitrary arrests, in order to crush strong and effective opposition and to prevent the Opposition from gaining State power. They resort to repressive action under the cloak and excuse of our wanting to depart from methods of constitutional struggle. But all Singapore, all South-East Asia, know the opposite is the case. We who are genuinely and consistently conducting a constitutional struggle, are continuously thwarted by those who resort to the most undemocratic and unconstitutional repressive measure. We are accused of wanting to depart from the path of constitutional struggle by those who resort to Fascist and unconstitutional methods of repression. It is like a robber, after he has committed a robbery, calling out, "Thief! Thief!"

    Let us take the argument put forward by the I.S.C. one stage further. Because of our open support for the Brunei uprising, so it is alleged that we want to depart from the path of constitutional struggle! I have already mentioned the feigned P.A.P. support of the Algerian people in their struggle for freedom. There was a hot war going on in Algeria with half a million French colons in the war. Did feigned P.A.P. support of the Algerian people in their war of liberation then make the P.A.P. depart from the constitutional struggle? Could we then say that the P.A.P. had embarked on the path of armed struggle? Of course not! No one would dream of saying so. Similarly our Barisan Sosialis support for the struggle of liberation in Brunei does not mean we are embarked on the path of armed struggle. It was only a token support to show our sympathy and admiration for the courage of the people of Brunei who refused to

Column: 447

be cowed by the superior might of a nuclear power. And we might add here that, as an Opposition Party, we in the Barisan Sosialis just cannot have the same opportunities and facilities for helping armed struggle anywhere. Now with bow and arrow, parangs, wooden-spears and shotguns, the people in Borneo are fighting against jets and warships for the cause of self-determination and freedom! And they are ready to fight against overwhelming odds because their will to be free cannot be suppressed by threats and superior force. If the P.A.P. support for the Algerian people's struggle is not regarded as embarking on unconstitutional and armed struggle, so is the Barisan Sosialis' open support for the Brunei people's struggle cannot be regarded as embarking on unconstitutional and armed struggle. Indeed, we maintain it is the only correct and proper thing to do if we are genuinely anti-colonial, and if we are truly dedicated to the struggle for justice, equality and democracy, peace and freedom.

    But let us take the argument just one stage further. When the West Irian issue was at fever pitch, and peace was threatened in South-East Asia, volunteers from Singapore were ready to go forward to help Indonesia recover West Irian. The P.A.P. had at first ridiculed the idea of resorting to armed struggle to drive out recalcitrant Dutch Imperialism in West Irian, simply because the initial call in Singapore for support of the Indonesian demand for the recovery of West Irian had come from the Barisan Sosialis. But the P.A.P. soon found itself in an embarrassing position. Realising that the vast majority of the people in Singapore had responded to our call and were supporting the demand for the recovery of West Irian, the P.A.P. was compelled to put on the anti-colonial mask. The P.A.P. was forced to support our motion calling for support of the Indonesian struggle to recover West Irian. Later in an attempt to make capital out of the anti-colonial fervour of the people in Singapore, P.A.P. Ministers went so far as to review volunteers about to fly off

Column: 448

for further training in Indonesia. P.A.P. Ministers gave them blessing and a rousing send-off. Full publicity was given to the Minister for Health and Law wishing the volunteers good luck at the Singapore Airport. If there was any talk of encouragement given to armed struggle, this was it. We do - not have to look any further. By I.S.C. standards, it could be said that encouragement to armed struggle was so blatant in this case that there is no point in the P.A.P. even trying to deny it.

    Yet the people of Singapore have never accused the P.A.P. of encouraging armed struggle. Neither have the British for that matter, so far as we know. It would have been silly, foolish and useless for them to do so. Yet today, without seeing any volunteer off, without in any way urging the people of Singapore to armed struggle, without in any way instigating disturbances, strikes or riots, we have been charged with wanting to resort to violence and bloodshed! How absurd and ridiculous can the P.A.P. become? What explanation can the P.A.P. give? As genuine anti-colonialists, we know that intransigent imperialists will never budge unless they are forced to do so. This was the case with Goa. This was the case with what was once called French Indo-China; and with what was once called the Dutch East Indies. And this again was the case with the West Irian issue. The intransigence of colonialists is proverbial. Look now what has happened in Brunei.

    The Brunei people have been deprived of all means of constitutional struggle. In spite of the Party Rakyat gaining all the 55 seats in the recent elections in Brunei, showing overwhelming support of the people, the elected representatives could only play the role of the Opposition. They were not permitted even to table a motion in the Council Negeri against Malaysia. Nor were they allowed to declare for independence. There were no longer any constitutional means left for the people of Brunei to oppose Malaysia. Under the circumstances, what else could the people of Brunei do? Submit to further oppression? No, Sir, there can be no doubt, no argument about it! All means of constitutional struggle were denied the

Column: 449

people of Brunei. There was but one way out. The Brunei uprising was the inevitable result. Is it then wrong to support such a heroic struggle under the circumstances? How can our support be twisted to mean our resorting to violence and bloodshed? Have not other Afro-Asian countries similarly supported the struggle of the people of Brunei? Of the people of Kalimantan Utara?

    Sir, all such talk of our wanting to resort to armed struggle is therefore so much hocus-pocus, meant only to confuse and deceive the people and to give an excuse to the British, the Federation and the P.A.P. to resort to repression. There is nothing that the Barisan Sosialis has done which the P.A.P. itself has not done but a short time ago. For the P.A.P. now to claim that what the Barisan Sosialis has done is unlawful is sheer unadulterated bunkum. It will not deceive anyone. This is only the colonial way of giving us a bad name and hanging us for it. So long as effective opposition to the P.A.P. can be removed, what matters what reason is given for its removal and how the P.A.P. does it? The ruthless and unscrupulous nature of the P.A.P. is already well known. The Barisan haunts the Prime Minister and his Ministers day and night. The Barisan has too much support for the comfort of the Prime Minister. Therefore, knocking out the Barisan has become an obsession with him.

    From all this, it is clear that excuses given by the I.S.C. and the P.A.P. for the arrests do not hold water. The Prime Minister said on 4th February:

    `If it were an action by the Singapore Government, we would never have contemplated it. It would not be necessary because we would have carried on till after 31st August, 1963.'

In this statement alone, Sir, the Prime Minister admits, albeit inadvertently, that there were no justifiable reasons whatsoever that necessitated the arrests. "It would not be necessary," he said. And this is confirmed in the Yang di-Pertuan Negara's speech which admits that "all was peace and tranquility" for the last seven months. Yet he now tells a story of Said Zahari having left Singapore on 1st February.

Column: 450



    Let us ask, then why did the P.A.P. carry out the arrests? I have already explained earlier on why the British and the Federation Government want to carry out the arrests. They want to protect their imperial vested interests. They want to destroy the Left-wing movement, if possible. But what of the P.A.P.? There is mention in the Yang di-Pertuan Negara's speech of the vested interests of the P.A.P. Government. What are these vested interests? What role do these vested interests play in the arrests?

    You will recall that the Prime Minister made some Press statements on his return from Kuala Lumpur after the arrests. The Member for Cairnhill had put the Prime Minister on the mat for having tried to pass the blame for the arrests on to the British and Federation Governments. He asked the Prime Minister, "Why did the P.A.P. Ministers not vote against the other members of the I.S.C. if they did not support the arrests?" And the poor Prime Minister had to eat humble pie and climb down and make a second statement to the Press, this time correcting his earlier statement and agreeing in toto with the I.S.C. decision.

    I have no wish to go into details, but it is already on record that all three parties concurred with the arrests. So the P.A.P. cannot possibly escape censure by trying to pass the buck this time. To understand P.A.P. vested interests and why they want the arrests, we must first understand the desperate situation in which the P.A.P. finds itself today. Soon after the assumption of power on the support of the workers in 1959, the arrogance, dictatorship, exposure and Rightist deviation of P.A.P. Ministers quickly alienated the Party away from the masses. Originally 43 in an Assembly of 51, their number soon dwindled to 40 in 1960; 39 in July 1961; and finally to 26, when 13 Assemblymen walked across the Floor to form the Barisan Sosialis.

days of yore for these arrogant men! The fear of our growing strength and influence is the urgent reason for the P.A.P. decision to try and cripple and paralyse the Barisan as much as possible. Hence the decision to arrest immediately and not after 31st August, 1963.

    The P.A.P. leaders hope that, with the Barisan crippled and generally disabled, the people would again be faced with a situation analagous to that existing at the time of the sham referendum.

    You will remember that the original referendum plot was to offer unacceptable alternatives to the people. They were to be compelled to choose the lesser of two or more evils. Similarly with the arrests, The P.A.P. leaders hope that a political vacuum, so to speak, would be created in the Singapore arena. And if there were no adequately organised political parties with sufficient mass support to eclipse the P.A.P. completely, the P.A.P. would still stand a chance of having some of their leaders again being elected to the Legislative Assembly. organisations, rural associations, hawkers associations, etc., will have to be dominated by pro-P.A.P. elements. That is why all the prominent leaders in these organisations have been arrested. The P.A.P. hopes to extend the sphere of P.A.P. influence into the other unions and organisations. This move is important for the immediate future. But, of course, these are only P.A.P. pipe-dreams.

Government - a matter of a P.A.P. Parliamentary Secretary attacking the P.A.P. Government! So what is the future going to be? We can only say that all the pipe-dreams of the P.A.P. will remain pipe-dreams. They go up like soap bubbles, and burst.

We still have the support of the workers and the civic organisations. And this support will enable the Barisan Sosialis to bury the P.A.P. when the time comes.

efforts to erect "standing monuments", according to the Prime Minister, in order to remind the people of the good work of the P.A.P. Government. And when the elections come along, they hope that these "standing monuments" will help to deceive the people and to win them their support.

    We must remember that, though the P.A.P. leaders might get away with not holding the Sembawang by-election, they will not be able to skip the general elections, that is, unless more funny things are cooking. The P.A.P. was elected for a five-year term. We have seen how desperately their Ministers cling to power on the slightest excuse. Their lust for power is so great that, if they could get away with it, they would most certainly do away with the coming general elections. But, alas, the gods are not with the Prime Minister. He cannot get away with it and there will have to be a general election at the latest in early 1964, and with every indication of it being held much earlier. We still know nothing though about how the 15 Central Parliament seats are to be filled. Similarly this time, since he has failed to win the support of the people in spite of all his tricks, he now attempts to intimidate them into supporting him. The ruthlessness of the P.A.P. is well known. If a P.A.P. member comes to ask for contribution towards the erection of welcome arches on the occasion of the Prime Minister's visit to a constituency, who can refuse and say no? When that fails, the next weapon is intimidation, and with the arrests, the Prime Minister
